recorded archeological site within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) perimeter of the Project Area (THC 2017),
while a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places (NRHP)
Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the NRHP
within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). The previously recorded archeological site and its
distance from the Project Area are summarized in Table 1 below, while its location relative to
the Project Area is presented in Figure 5. No documented cultural resources, including any
listed on the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the Project Area. Based on

the current Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on an
elevated landform above Halamicek Draw, in conjunction with a previously recorded prehistoric
site only a short distance to the northwest, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that
there existed a moderate to high potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within
the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
26 April 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 3 shovel tests per acre for projects measuring between 0 and 3.0 acres in size. As
the Project Area totals approximately 0.6 acres, a minimum of 2 shovel tests were necessary
within the Project Area. Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by excavating a total of 3 shovel tests
within the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter
[mm]) hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening.
The locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 7. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 3.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
3 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
55 to Block 54 (Area C) South Connector Surface Site on GLO property will have no adverse
effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as
SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the
development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely

event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Block 55 (Area C) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Block 55 (Area C)
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, a
portion of the Project Area is located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 8.7 miles (14.0 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Anderson Ranch, Texas, Mentone SW, Texas, and Halamicek Ranch, Texas, topographic
quadrangle maps. The Project Area consists of pipeline ROWs that measures approximately
7.1 miles (11.4 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide (approximately 25.8 acres).
However, only approximately 4.0 miles (6.4 km; 14.5 acres) of the Project Area is located on
GLO land.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above Halamicek, McCarty, and Smith draws, and their tributaries, in
conjunction with the presence of a previously recorded prehistoric site within the review
perimeter, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a moderate to high
potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project
Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 2-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
3 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface shovel
tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 4.0 miles (6.4 km) in
length, a minimum of 64 shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the proposed ROW.
Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by excavating a total of 72 shovel tests within the Project Area.
All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh
or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the
excavated shovel tests are presented on Figures 7 and 8. Shovel test data are presented in
Table 3.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in the documentation of 1 new
prehistoric lithic scatter within the extreme southern extent of the Project Area. This site,
41RV116, is summarized below.
Site 41RV116

portion of the Project Area, approximately 600.0 feet (183.0 m) northeast of previously recorded

site 41RV107 (Figures 9 and 10). It is situated on the southern slope of a small rise just to the
north of Halamicek Draw. The location, just east of an existing lease road, has a gravel-covered
and deflated erosional surface spotted with scattered sagebrush, mesquite, creosote, and
various cacti (Figures 11 and 12). Surface visibility across the site ranged from 75% to 100%.
A total of 9 shovel tests were excavated across this site along the proposed ROW. All 9
produced negative results for subsurface cultural materials.

9 May 2017

Page 19

Observed Cultural Materials
The cultural materials observed on site 41RV116 consisted of roughly 30 lithic flakes of chert,
fine-grained quartzite, and chalcedony, along with several biface and uniface fragments (Figure
13). No formal tools or fire-cracked rock (FCR) were noted on the site that would reflect the
use of the location as a campsite. Rather, the presence of available gravels on the erosional
surface of the site and an abundance of specimens reflecting the early stages of the lithic
reduction process suggest that the location likely served as source of raw lithic materials.
Cultural Features
No cultural features were observed on the surface of site 41RV116, and no evidence of any
subsurface cultural features was noted within any of the 9 shovel tests excavated across the
site.
Horizontal and Vertical Extents of the Cultural Materials
Based on the extent of the observed surface materials, the assessed horizontal extent of the
site measures approximately 328.1 feet (100.0 m) north to south by 246.1 feet (75.0 m) east to
west.
All observed cultural materials were noted on the erosional surface of the site. No evidence of
subsurface cultural deposits was noted within any of the 9 shovel tests excavated across the
site.
Summary
Site 41RV116 was documented as a moderate-density prehistoric lithic scatter on a small rise to
the north of Halamicek Draw. Chert, fine-grained quartzite, and chalcedony gravels on the
erosional surface of the site provided a source of raw lithic material that was exploited by the
aboriginal occupants of the region. This is evidenced by the variety of early stage lithic flaking
debris scattered over the surface of the site. The absence of any formal tools, FCR, or cultural
features on the site suggested that it did not double as a campsite.
Site 41RV116 is located approximately 600.0 feet (183.0 m) northeast of previously recorded
site 41RV107. Despite their relative proximity, no cultural materials were observed on the
surface between these 2 locations, indicating that they are separate sites rather than 1 larger
site.
Based on: 1) the surficial nature of the observed cultural deposits; 2) the lack of buried, stratified
cultural deposits; and 3) the lack of any temporally diagnostic materials on the site, it is
Horizon’s opinion that site 41RV116 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL. With this in
mind, it is Horizon’s further opinion that no additional investigations are warranted on site
41RV116 in connection with the currently proposed undertaking.

HJN 160006 AR 46
9 May 2017
Page 20

Figure 13. View of lithic specimens on site 41RV116
Recommendations
Based on the assessment that site 41RV116 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL, it is
Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block 55 (Area C) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline
ROWs across GLO property will have no adverse effect on significant cultural resources
designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs. Horizon therefore recommends
that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of the Project Area relative to the
jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any cultural materials (including
human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at any point during construction,
use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the proposed undertaking, even in previously
surveyed areas, all work at the location of the discovery should cease immediately, and the
THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated

RE:

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Chalk Bluff (Area C) Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 47

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Chalk Bluff (Area C)
Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project
Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,
portions of the Project Area are located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 10.4 miles (16.7 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Narrow Bow Draw, Texas, and Halamicek Ranch, Texas, topographic quadrangle maps. The
Project Area consists of a pipeline ROW that measures approximately 3.2 miles (5.1 km) long
by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide (approximately 11.5 acres). However, only approximately 1.1
miles (1.7 km; 3.9 acres) of the Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) perimeter of the Project
Area (THC 2017). Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of
Historic Places (NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties
listed on the NRHP within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). No documented cultural resources,
including any listed on the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries
of the Project Area. Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have
been undertaken with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is a prehistoric campsite. This
site, 41RV107, is located approximately 1.5 miles (2.5 km) south of the Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above John D Draw, McCarty Draw, and their tributaries, it was Horizon’s
opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for undocumented
prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
26 April 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 1.1 miles (1.7 km) in
length, a minimum of 17 shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the proposed ROW.
Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a total of 17 shovel tests within the Project Area. All
excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh or
were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the
excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
17 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Chalk
Bluff (Area C) Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects across GLO property will have no
adverse effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for
designation as SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with
the development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the
unlikely event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are
inadvertently discovered at any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within

Emerald City Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 49

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Emerald City Corridor
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,
portions of the Project Area are located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 3.4 miles (5.5 kilometers [km])
southeast of Orla, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute Orla
SE, Texas topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline ROW that
measures approximately 3.8 miles (6.1 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 13.8 acres). However, only approximately 2721.0 feet (829.6 m; 1.9 acres) of
the Project Area is located on GLO land (maps.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of 7 previously
recorded archeological sites within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) perimeter of the Project Area (THC
2017), while a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). The previously recorded archeological sites and
their distances from the Project Area are summarized in Table 1 below, while their locations
relative to the Project Area are presented in Figure 5.

Of the 7 previously recorded archeological sites within the review perimeter, site 41RV92 is
crossed by the current Project Area. This site is a segment of a historic-era roadbed with
associated utility poles. When originally recorded, it was assessed as being ineligible for
inclusion on the NRHP. The portion of this site crossed by the current Project Area is located
on private property where no federal nexus exists. As such, it will not be reassessed as part of
the current investigations that focus solely on GLO land. Based on the Atlas database, no
previous cultural resources surveys are mapped within the boundaries of the current Project
Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above Sand Bend Draw and a tributary of the Pecos River, in conjunction
with the presence of several previously recorded prehistoric sites within the review perimeter, it
was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for
undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 4-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
12 July 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 2721.0 feet (829.6
m) in length, a minimum of 8 shovel tests shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the
proposed ROW. Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by excavating a total of 9 shovel tests within
the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm])
hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The
locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 7. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 3.

Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
9 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Emerald
City Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline ROWs across GLO property will have no adverse
effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as
SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the
development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely
event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently
discovered at any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the
proposed undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the
discovery should cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and

HJN 160006 AR 49
13 July 2017

recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to call or email me.
Sincerely,

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Block 55 to 54 (Area
C) South Corridor Droop Mountain Lateral rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas
(Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded.
However, it is located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO
is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls under the regulations
of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton)
has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural
resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey
was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the Project Area and, if any
existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites
considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon
conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC)
annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 12.9 miles (20.7 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Mentone SW, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline
ROW that measures approximately 867.0 feet (264.3 meters [m]) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 m) wide
(approximately 0.6 acres). The entirety of the Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on an
elevated landform above Halamicek Draw, in conjunction with the presence of a previously
recorded prehistoric site within the review perimeter, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field
efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural
deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
26 April 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals only 867.0 feet (264.3 m) in length,
a minimum of 3 shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the proposed ROW. Horizon
met the TSMASS by excavating a total of 3 shovel tests within the Project Area. All excavated
matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh or were trowelsorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the excavated
shovel tests are presented on Figure 7. Shovel test data are presented in Table 3.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
3 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
55 to 54 (Area C) South Corridor Droop Mountain Lateral across GLO property will have no
adverse effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for
designation as SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with
the development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the

Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Block 55-55 - Block 2 CTF Junction Surface Site Project

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Block 55-55 - Block 2
CTF Junction Surface Site Project in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The
development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, the Project Area is located
on property owned by the Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a
political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls under the regulations of the Antiquities
Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted
with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of
the Project Area in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if
any archeological sites were located within the Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if
the project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal
designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources
investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 8.4 miles (13.5 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Anderson Ranch, Texas topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a small
surface site that measures approximately 2.1 acres in size. It is located entirely on GLO land.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Internet at the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s)
Texas Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) website indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) radius of the Project Area.
Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter. No documented cultural resources, including any listed on
the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries of the Project Area.
Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have been undertaken
with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is a prehistoric campsite. This
site, 41RV49, is located approximately 3.8 miles (6.2 km) northeast of the Project Area.
Soils
Two soil types are mapped within the Project Area. These soils are summarized in Table 1
(NRCS 1980) and presented Figure 5.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on an
elevated landform above a tributary of Smith Draw, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field
efforts that there existed a moderate potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits
within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
18 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 3 shovel tests per acre for projects measuring between 0 and 3.0 acres in size. As
the Project Area totals approximately 2.1 acres, a minimum of 6 shovel tests were necessary
within the Project Area. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a total of 6 shovel tests within
the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm])
hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The
locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
6 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
55-55 - Block 2 CTF Junction Surface Site on GLO property will have no adverse effect on
significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Fort Pillow 54-4-13 1H Flowline ROW
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 52

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Fort Pillow 54-4-13 1H
Flowline right-of-way (ROW) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The
development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, the Project Area is located
on property owned by the Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a
political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls under the regulations of the Antiquities
Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted
with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of
the Project Area in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if
any archeological sites were located within the Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if
the project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal
designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources
investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 7.7 miles (12.4 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Mentone SW, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline
ROW that measures approximately 1.0 mile (1.6 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 3.6 acres). It is located entirely on GLO land.

Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter. No documented cultural resources, including any listed on
the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries of the Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above several unnamed drainages, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field
efforts that there existed at least a moderate potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural
deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
18 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the Project Area totals approximately 1.0 mile (1.6 km) in length, a minimum of 16
shovel tests were necessary within the Project Area. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a
total of 16 shovel tests within the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through
0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils
prohibited successful screening. The locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on
Figure 6. Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
16 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
55-55 - Block 2 CTF Junction Surface Site on GLO property will have no adverse effect on
significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Lexington Corridor
(Area C) Oil, Gas, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project
Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, a
portion of the Project Area is located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 13.3 miles (21.4 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Halamicek Ranch, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline
ROW that measures approximately3.2 miles (5.1 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 11.6 acres). However, only approximately 360.0 feet (109.7 m; 0.2 acre) of the
Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above Halamicek Draw and tributaries of McIlvain Draw, in conjunction with
the presence of a previously recorded prehistoric site within the review perimeter, it was
Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for
undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on

minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 360.0 feet (109.7 m)

proposed ROW. Horizon exceed the TSMASS by excavating a total of 3 shovel tests within the
Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm])
hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The
locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 7. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 3.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
3 excavated shovel tests.

RE:

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Mako State 2-34 Frac Pond to Laramie 55-4-7 Frac Pond Water Transfer
Pipeline ROW
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 54

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Mako State 2-34 Frac
Pond to Laramie 55-4-7 Frac Pond Water Transfer Pipeline right-of-way (ROW) in Reeves
County, Texas (Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be
privately funded. However, a portion of the Project Area is located on property owned by the
Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the
state, the undertaking falls under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On
behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental
Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance
with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were
located within the Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to
have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State
Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under
Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 6.7 miles (10.8 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Anderson Ranch, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline
ROW that measures approximately 6.2 miles (10.0 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 22.5 acres). However, only approximately 4555.3 feet (1388.5 m; 3.1 acres) of
the Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) radius of the Project Area.
Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter. No documented cultural resources, including any listed on
the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries of the Project Area.
Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have been undertaken
with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is a prehistoric campsite. The
centroid of this site, 41RV49, is located approximately 2.0 miles (3.3 km) northeast of the
Project Area.
Soils
A total of 3 soil types are mapped within the Project Area. These soils are summarized in Table
1 (NRCS 1980) and presented Figure 5.
Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on an
elevated landform above Smith Draw, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there
existed at least a moderate potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the
boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
17 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 4555.3 feet (1388.5

HJN 160006 AR 54
23 May 2017

Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm])
hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The
locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 2.

Site 41RV119
General Description
Site 41RV119 is a newly recorded prehistoric lithic scatter. It is situated within a relatively flat,
upland desert setting, approximately 1500.00 feet (457.2 m) south of an unnamed tributary of
Smith Draw (Figures 7 and 8). The location is spanned by an existing lease road approximately
0.4 miles (0.6 km) southwest of US Highway (Hwy) 285. The site has a gravel-covered and
deflated erosional surface spotted with scattered sagebrush, mesquite, creosote, and various
cacti (Figures 9 and 10). Surface visibility across the site ranged from 75% to 100%. A total of
7 shovel tests were excavated across this site along the proposed ROW. All 7 produced
negative results for subsurface cultural materials.
Observed Cultural Materials
The cultural materials observed on site 41RV119 consisted of roughly 25 chert flakes (primary,
secondary, and tertiary), as well as 1 tested chert cobble (Figures 11 and 12). No formal tools
or fire-cracked rock (FCR) were noted on the site that would reflect the use of the location as a
campsite. Rather, the presence of available gravels on the erosional surface of the site and an
abundance of specimens reflecting the early stages of the lithic reduction process suggest that
the location likely served as source of raw lithic materials.
Cultural Features
No cultural features were observed on the surface of site 41RV119, and no evidence of any
subsurface cultural features was noted within any of the 7 shovel tests excavated across the
site.
Horizontal and Vertical Extents of the Cultural Materials
Based on the extent of the observed surface materials, the assessed horizontal extent of the
site measures approximately 426.5 feet (130.0 m) northeast to southwest by 164.0 feet (50.0 m)
northwest to southeast.
All observed cultural materials were noted on the erosional surface of the site. No evidence of
subsurface cultural deposits was noted within any of the 7 shovel tests excavated across the
site.

Page 15

Summary
Site 41RV119 was documented as a moderate-density prehistoric lithic scatter within a
generally featureless desert upland to the south of a tributary of Smith Draw. Gravels on the
erosional surface of the site appear to have provided a source of raw lithic material that was
exploited by the aboriginal occupants of the region. This is evidenced by the variety of early
stage lithic flaking debris scattered over the surface of the site. The absence of any formal
tools, FCR, or cultural features on the site suggested that it did not double as a campsite.
Based on: 1) the surficial nature of the observed cultural deposits; 2) the lack of buried, stratified
cultural deposits; and 3) the lack of any temporally diagnostic materials on the site, it is
Horizon’s opinion that site 41RV119 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL. With this in
mind, it is Horizon’s further opinion that no additional investigations are warranted on site
41RV119 in connection with the currently proposed undertaking.
Recommendations
Based on the assessment that site 41RV119 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL, it is
Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Mako State 2-34 Frac Pond to Laramie 55-4-7
Frac Pond Water Transfer Pipeline ROW across GLO property will have no adverse effect on
significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any
cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at
any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the proposed
undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the discovery should
cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to call or email me.
Sincerely,
For Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on a
prominent landform between tributaries of Threemile Draw, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the
field efforts that there existed a moderate potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural
deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.

HJN 160006 AR 55
23 May 2017
Page 6

Figure 5. Soils mapped within the Project Area

HJN 160006 AR 55
23 May 2017
Page 7

In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
17 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 3 shovel tests per acre for projects measuring between 0 and 3.0 acres in size. As
the Project Area totals approximately 0.5 acres, a minimum of 2 shovel tests were necessary
within the Project Area. Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by excavating a total of 6 shovel tests
within the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter
[mm]) hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening.
The locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
6 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
57-57 to 56 South Connector Junction Surface Site on GLO property will have no adverse effect
on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any
cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at
any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the proposed
undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the discovery should
cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Kaycee Corridor and Gas, Oil, and SWD Lateral Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 56

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Kaycee Corridor and
Gas, Oil, and SWD Lateral rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, a
portion of the Project Area is located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 11.2 miles (18.0 kilometers [km])
southwest of Orla, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Threemile Draw, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline
ROW that measures approximately 1974.6 feet (601.9 meters [m]) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 m)
wide (approximately 1.4 acres). However, only approximately 1152.1 feet (351.2 m; 0.8 acre) of
the Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) radius of the Project Area.
Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter. No documented cultural resources, including any listed on
the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries of the Project Area.
Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have been undertaken
with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area has no associated site form on
the Atlas database. This site, 41RV59, is located approximately 5.2 miles (8.4 km) southeast of
the Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the distance of the Project Area from
extant water courses, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a
relatively low potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of
the Project Area.

historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the

Field Survey
Methodology
A 3-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
17 May 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 1152.1 feet (351.2
m) in length, a minimum of 4 shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the proposed
ROW. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a total of 4 shovel tests within the Project Area.
All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh
or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the
excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
4 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Kaycee
Corridor and Gas, Oil, and SWD Lateral ROWs across GLO property will have no adverse effect
on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any
cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at
any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the proposed
undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the discovery should
cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.

Anadarko Petroleum Corporation

Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Reeves Oil Pipeline
Phase I and Block 56 (Area B) to Block 55 (Area C) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way
(ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development of the
Project Area will be privately funded. However, portions of the Project Area are located on
property owned by the Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a
political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls under the regulations of the Antiquities
Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted
with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of
the Project Area in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if
any archeological sites were located within the Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if
the project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal
designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources
investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 8.3 miles (13.4 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Narrow Bow Draw, Texas, and Anderson Ranch, Texas, topographic quadrangle maps. The
Project Area consists of a pipeline ROW that measures approximately 10.3 miles (16.6 km) long
by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide (approximately 37.5 acres). However, only approximately 1.5
miles (2.4 km; 5.5 acres) of the Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above Narrow Bow Draw, Horsehead Draw, their tributaries, and tributaries
of the Pecos River, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a
moderate to high potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries
of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 4-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
12 July 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 1.5 miles (2.4 km) in
length, a minimum of 24 shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the proposed ROW.
Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by excavating a total of 31 shovel tests within the Project Area.
All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh
or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the
excavated shovel tests are presented on Figures 6 and 7. Shovel test data are presented in
Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in the documentation of 1 new
prehistoric lithic scatter within the extreme southern extent of the Project Area. This site,
41RV120, is summarized below.
Site 41RV120
General Description
Site 41RV120 is a newly recorded prehistoric lithic scatter recorded within the southern portion
of the Project Area. It is situated on the east-facing gentle slope of a small rise just to the
northwest of Horsehead Draw. The location is part of an active oil field, with a well pad to the
north; several rigs to the west; access roads running to the north, south, and east; and multiple

pre-existing underground pipelines (Figures 8 to 10). Vegetation consists of mesquite,
blackbrush, creosote bush, cenizo, pickleweed, seepweed, sand sagebrush, prickly pear cactus,
Chistmas cactus, tasajillo, yucca, and various short clump grasses. Surface visibility across the
site ranged from 90% to 100%. A total of 6 shovel tests were excavated across this site along
the proposed ROW. All 6 produced negative results for subsurface cultural materials.
Observed Cultural Materials
The cultural materials observed on site 41RV120 consisted of a low-density scatter of a tested
cobble (possibly rhyolite), 1 edge-modified flake tool manufactured from gray chert, and chert
debitage (Figure 11). No formal tools or fire-cracked rock (FCR) were noted on the site that
would reflect the use of the location as a campsite. Rather, the presence of available gravels on
the erosional surface of the site suggests that the location likely served as source of raw lithic
materials.
Cultural Features
No cultural features were observed on the surface of site 41RV120, and no evidence of any
subsurface cultural features was noted within any of the 6 shovel tests excavated across the
site.
Horizontal and Vertical Extents of the Cultural Materials
Based on the extent of the observed surface materials, the assessed horizontal extent of the
site measures approximately 154.2 feet (47.0 m) north to south by 328.0 feet (100.0 m) east to
west.

HJN 160006 AR 57
13 July 2017

41RV120

HJN 160006 AR 57

Figure 11. View of lithic artifacts observed on site 41RV120

HJN 160006 AR 57
13 July 2017
Page 15

All observed cultural materials were noted on the erosional surface of the site. No evidence of
subsurface cultural deposits was noted within any of the 6 shovel tests excavated across the
site.
Summary
Site 41RV120 was documented as a low-density prehistoric lithic scatter on the gradual slope of
a small rise to the northwest of Horsehead Draw. Chert and possibly rhyolite gravels on the
erosional surface of the site provided a source of raw lithic material that was exploited by the
aboriginal occupants of the region. This is evidenced by the variety of early stage lithic flaking
debris scattered over the surface of the site. The absence of any formal tools, FCR, or cultural
features on the site suggested that it did not double as a campsite.
Based on: 1) the surficial nature of the observed cultural deposits; 2) the lack of buried, stratified
cultural deposits; and 3) the lack of any temporally diagnostic materials on the site, it is
Horizon’s opinion that site 41RV120 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL. With this in
mind, it is Horizon’s further opinion that no additional investigations are warranted on site
41RV120 in connection with the currently proposed undertaking.
Recommendations
Based on the assessment that site 41RV120 is ineligible for formal designation as a SAL, it is
Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Reeves Oil Pipeline Phase I and Block 56 (Area B)
to Block 55 (Area C) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline ROWs across GLO property will have no
adverse effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for
designation as SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with
the development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the
unlikely event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are
inadvertently discovered at any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within
the limits of the proposed undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the
location of the discovery should cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of
the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Block 55 - Chalk Bluff Junction Site Project
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 58

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Block 55 - Chalk Bluff
Junction Site Project in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area; Figures 1 to 4). The development
of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, the Project Area is located on property
owned by the Texas General Land Office (GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political
subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of
Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko, Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with
Horizon Environmental Services, Inc. (Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the
Project Area in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if any
archeological sites were located within the Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the
project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal
designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources
investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 12.1 miles (19.5 kilometers [km])
southwest of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Halamicek Ranch, Texas topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a small
surface site that measures approximately 0.3 acre in size. It is located entirely on GLO land.

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Internet at the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s)
Texas Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) website indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) radius of the Project Area.
Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places
(NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the
NRHP within the review perimeter. No documented cultural resources, including any listed on
the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries of the Project Area.
Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have been undertaken
with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is a prehistoric campsite. This
site, 41RV107, is located approximately 1.5 miles (2.4 km) south of the Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on an
elevated landform above several vegetated drainages linked to Smith Draw, it was Horizon’s
opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a moderate potential for undocumented
prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.

13 July 2017

Page 7

In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 4-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
13 July 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 3 shovel tests per acre for projects measuring between 0 and 3.0 acres in size. As
the Project Area totals approximately 0.3 acre, a minimum of 1 shovel tests was necessary
within the Project Area. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating 1 shovel test within the Project
Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware
mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The location of
the excavated shovel test is presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within the 1 excavated
shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Block
55 - Chalk Bluff Junction Site on GLO property will have no adverse effect on significant cultural
resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs. Horizon therefore
recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of the Project Area
relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any cultural materials
(including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at any point during
construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the proposed undertaking, even in
previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the discovery should cease immediately,
and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Seahawk Corridor
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,
portions of the Project Area are located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the

adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities

Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under

Project Description
