northwest of Orla, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Orla, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of a pipeline ROW that
measures approximately 3.3 miles (5.3 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 12.0 acres). However, only approximately 694.9 feet (212.8 m; 0.5 acre) of the
Project Area is located on GLO land.

RE:

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Bell Town Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 60

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Bell Town Corridor
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,
portions of the Project Area are located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 7.3 miles (11.7 kilometers [km])
southwest of Orla, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Derrick Draw, Texas, and Threemile Draw, Texas topographic quadrangle maps. The Project
Area consists of a pipeline ROW that measures approximately 6.8 miles (11.0 km) long by 30.0
feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide (approximately 24.7 acres). However, only approximately 2.5 miles
(3.9 km; 9.1 acres) of the Project Area is located on GLO land.
CORPORATE HEADQUARTERS
1507 S Interstate 35  Austin, TX 78741-2502  (512) 328-2430  www.horizon-esi.com
An LJA Company

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of no previously
recorded archeological sites or cemeteries within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) perimeter of the Project
Area (THC 2017). Similarly, a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of
Historic Places (NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties
listed on the NRHP within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). No documented cultural resources,
including any listed on the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the boundaries
of the Project Area. Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys have
been undertaken with the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is a prehistoric lithic procurement
area. This site, 41RV105, is located approximately 5.5 miles (8.9 km) north of the Project Area.
Soils
A total of 3 soil types are mapped within the Project Area. These soils are summarized in Table
1 (NRCS 1980) and presented Figure 5.
Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
prominent landforms above Incline and Threemile draws, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the
field efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural
deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 4-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
12 July 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in

Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
40 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Bell
Town Corridor Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects across GLO property will have no adverse

HJN 160006 AR 60
13 July 2017
Page 11

effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as
SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the
development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely
event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently
discovered at any point during construction, use, or ongoing maintenance within the limits of the
proposed undertaking, even in previously surveyed areas, all work at the location of the
discovery should cease immediately, and the THC and GLO should be notified of the discovery.
On behalf of Anadarko and Whitenton, Horizon is seeking documented consultation with your
office in compliance with the ACT.
Should you concur with Horizon’s findings and
recommendations, please sign below and return. Again, this letter serves as an interim report
for consultation purposes. The results of these investigations will eventually be incorporated
into a formal report that includes the results of all cultural resources investigations conducted
under TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to call or email me.

Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,

(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas

Project Area is located on GLO land.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on

cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 4-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the Project Area for cultural resources on
13 July 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection and the excavation of subsurface
shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey Standards (TSMASS) require a
minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in
width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land totals approximately 0.7 miles (1.1 km) in
length, a minimum of 11 shovel tests shovel tests were necessary along this portion of the
proposed ROW. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a total of 11 shovel tests within the
Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm])
hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited successful screening. The
locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 7. Shovel test data are
presented in Table 3.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the Project Area resulted in entirely negative findings. No
cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area or within any of the
11 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Mariner
Corridor (Area A) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline ROWs across GLO property will have no adverse
effect on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as
SALs. Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the
development of the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely
event that any cultural materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently

RE:

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Block 57 (Area A) Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline Projects
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 62

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Block 57 (Area A)
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However,
portions of the Project Area are located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the Project Area in compliance with the ACT.
The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological sites were located within the
Project Area and, if any existed, to determine if the project had the potential to have any
adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal designation as State Antiquities
Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources investigations under Texas
Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 3.0 miles (4.9 kilometers [km])
west of Orla, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute Red
Bluff, Texas, Orla, Texas, and Threemile Draw, Texas topographic quadrangle maps. The
Project Area consists of a pipeline ROW that measures approximately 27.5 miles (44.4 km) long
by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide (approximately 100.0 acres). However, only approximately
1.1 miles (1.7 km; 4.0 acres) of the Project Area is located on GLO land.

An LJA Company

Archival Research
Archival research conducted via the Texas Historical Commission’s (THC’s) Texas
Archeological Sites Atlas (Atlas) online database indicated the presence of 1 previously
recorded archeological site within a 1.0-mile (1.6-km) perimeter of the Project Area (THC 2017),
while a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of Historic Places (NRHP)
Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties listed on the NRHP
within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). The previously recorded archeological site and its
distance from the Project Area are summarized in Table 1 below, while its location relative to
the Project Area is presented in Figure 5.

The Project Area extends across the 1 previously recorded archeological site within the review
perimeter. This site, 41LV15 is a prehistoric lithic procurement area that has an overall
undetermined NRHP eligibility status. The portion of this site crossed by the current Project
Area is located on private property where no federal nexus exists. As such, it will not be
reassessed as part of the current investigations that focus solely on GLO land. Based on the
Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys are mapped within the boundaries of the
current Project Area.
Soils
A total of 2 soil types are mapped within the Project Area. These soils are summarized in Table
2 (NRCS 1980) and presented Figure 6.
Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above Salt Creek, its tributaries, and Sand Bend and Threemile draws, it
was Horizon’s opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed a high potential for
undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.

on significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.

the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
elevated landforms above a tributary of the Pecos River, it was Horizon’s opinion prior to the
field efforts that there existed a moderate to high potential for undocumented prehistoric cultural
deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 2-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the portion of the Project Area on GLO
land for cultural resources on 26 September 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection
and the excavation of subsurface shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey
Standards (TSMASS) require a minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects
measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land
totals approximately 936.0 feet (285.3 m) in length, a minimum of 3 shovel tests were necessary
along this portion of the proposed ROW. Horizon met the TSMASS by excavating a total of
3 shovel tests within the Project Area. All excavated matrices were screened through 0.25-inch
(6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense clay soils prohibited
successful screening. The locations of the excavated shovel tests are presented on Figure 6.
Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the portion of the Project Area on GLO land resulted in entirely
negative findings. No cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area on
GLO land or within any of the 3 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the
Fredericksburg 3-8 Unit 1H Flowline ROW across GLO land will have no adverse effect on
significant cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs.
Horizon therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of
the Project Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any

Interim Report
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation
Cholla State 2-4 2H Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline ROWs
Reeves County, Texas
Antiquities Code of Texas (GLO) – TAC Permit No. 7883
HJN 160006 AR 72

Mr. Wolfe:
Anadarko Petroleum Corporation (Anadarko) is proposing to develop the Cholla State 2-4 2H
Gas, Oil, and SWD Pipeline rights-of-way (ROWs) in Reeves County, Texas (Project Area;
Figures 1 to 4). The development of the Project Area will be privately funded. However, a
portion of the Project Area is located on property owned by the Texas General Land Office
(GLO). As the GLO is considered to be a political subdivision of the state, the undertaking falls
under the regulations of the Antiquities Code of Texas (ACT). On behalf of Anadarko,
Whitenton Group (Whitenton) has contracted with Horizon Environmental Services, Inc.
(Horizon) to conduct a cultural resources survey of the portion of the Project Area on GLO land
in compliance with the ACT. The purpose of the survey was to determine if any archeological
sites were located within the Project Area on GLO land and, if any existed, to determine if the
project had the potential to have any adverse impacts on sites considered eligible for formal
designation as State Antiquities Landmarks (SALs). Horizon conducted the cultural resources
investigations under Texas Antiquities Committee (TAC) annual permit number 7883.
This interim report summarizes Horizon’s findings and serves as a management tool for
consultation purposes regarding the Project Area. The results of these investigations will
eventually be compiled into a formal report that will incorporate all projects completed under
TAC annual permit number 7883 during the 2017 calendar year.
Project Description
The Project Area is located in Reeves County, approximately 6.0 miles (9.7 kilometers [km])
west of Mentone, Texas. It can be found on the US Geological Survey (USGS) 7.5-minute
Anderson Ranch, Texas, topographic quadrangle map. The Project Area consists of pipeline
ROWs that measure approximately 3540.0 (1079.0 km) long by 30.0 feet (9.1 meters [m]) wide
(approximately 2.4 acres). However, only approximately 1751.2 feet (533.8 m; 1.2 acres) of the
Project Area is located on GLO land.

Area (THC 2017). Similarly a review of the National Park Service’s (NPS) National Register of
Historic Places (NRHP) Google Earth map layer indicated the presence of no historic properties
listed on the NRHP within the review perimeter (NPS 2017). No documented cultural resources,
including any listed on the NRHP, are located within or immediately adjacent to the Project
Area. Based on the Atlas database, no previous cultural resources surveys are mapped within
the boundaries of the current Project Area.
The closest documented cultural resource to the Project Area is an extensive prehistoric
campsite. This site, 41RV49, is located approximately 3.1 miles (5.0 km) southeast of the
Project Area.

Archeological Probability Assessment
Prehistoric archeological sites are commonly found in upland areas and on alluvial terraces near
stream/river channels or drainages. Additionally, in this part of the state, they are often found in
proximity to playa lakebeds and dune blowouts. Based on the location of the Project Area on
terraces adjacent to tributaries of Horsehead Draw and the Pecos River, it was Horizon’s
opinion prior to the field efforts that there existed at least a moderate potential for
undocumented prehistoric cultural deposits within the boundaries of the Project Area.
In regard to historic-era resources, the lack of visible structures in immediate proximity to the
Project Area on the relevant topographic quadrangle map suggested a decreased potential for
historic-era standing structures or associated cultural deposits within the boundaries of the
Project Area.
Field Survey
Methodology
A 2-person Horizon archeological field crew assessed the portion of the Project Area on GLO
land for cultural resources on 26 September 2017. This entailed intensive surface inspection
and the excavation of subsurface shovel tests. The Texas State Minimum Archeological Survey
Standards (TSMASS) require a minimum of 16 shovel tests per mile for linear projects
measuring up to 100.0 feet (30.5 m) in width. As the portion of the Project Area on GLO land
totals approximately 1751.2 feet (533.8 m) in length, a minimum of 5 shovel tests were
necessary along this portion of the proposed ROW. Horizon exceeded the TSMASS by
excavating a total of 6 shovel tests within the Project Area. All excavated matrices were
screened through 0.25-inch (6.4-millimeter [mm]) hardware mesh or were trowel-sorted if dense
clay soils prohibited successful screening. The locations of the excavated shovel tests are
presented on Figure 6. Shovel test data are presented in Table 2.
Results
The cultural resources survey of the portion of the Project Area on GLO land resulted in entirely
negative findings. No cultural materials were observed on the surface of the Project Area on
GLO land or within any of the 6 excavated shovel tests.
Recommendations
Based on the negative survey results, it is Horizon’s opinion that the construction of the Beans
Station 53-4-5 1H Flowline ROW across GLO land will have no adverse effect on significant
cultural resources designated as or considered eligible for designation as SALs. Horizon
therefore recommends that Anadarko be allowed to proceed with the development of the Project
Area relative to the jurisdiction of the ACT. However, in the unlikely event that any cultural
materials (including human remains or burial features) are inadvertently discovered at any point

The review staff led by David Camarena and Justin Kockritz has completed its review and has made the
following determinations based on the information submitted for review:
Above-Ground Resources
• No historic properties present or affected
Archeology Comments
• No effect on archeological sites. However, if buried cultural materials are encountered during
construction or disturbance activities, work should cease in the immediate area; work can continue
where no cultural materials are present. Please contact the THC's Archeology Division at 512-463-6096
to consult on further actions that may be necessary to protect the cultural remains.
